21/05/2023, 8:34 pm - Aggie: Security Advisory
 *SCOPOLAMINE POWDER AKA DEVIL'S BREATH - BEWARE DEAR ONES!!!*

Robbery without   violence has become too common on the streets of Nairobi and other towns. 

They use Scopolamine powder to immobilize their victims. 

 Scopolamine is an anti-nauseant drug medically used for motion sickness. It is nowadays commonly being abused to waylay innocent people in Nairobi and other parts of the country. 

It can be blown to your face, placed on your skin during a handshake or given to you soaked in a business card. Its effects are nearly immediate. You become dizzy, weak, vision becomes blurry, you get zombified, confused and lastly lose free will. 

They majorly bank on the last. You will give out your bank PINs plus ATMs, your money in the pockets/purse and mpesa transfer with your full knowledge without being coerced to do so. They may tell you to do anything and you will do without questioning them back. They will rape you and you will not fight back. Later on when you recover from its effects you will have no memory of what happened.

*Security Guidelines for you  !!!!*
1 - Do not stand with strangers you don't know. Be aware of your surroundings !!!!
2 - Do not engage  with strangers who pretend talking to you.
3 - DON'T WALK ALONE IN TOWN especially high risk areas that you are alone  (if possible). 
4 - Do not offer to give directions when asked of especially the person asking wants you to personally take him or her there.
5 - Do not leave food or a drink unattended to while going to the long or even for short call. Should you leave, let someone you trust take charge of your drink.
6 - Always have a high index of suspicion; the robbers are usually well dressed women and men. You will least suspect.
7 - Walk fast in town to the specific place you are headed. Stop idling as you may be a good target.
8 - Even while driving through crowds like in popular "matatu stage", always be alert; as they may spray this while you are on jam.
9 - When using PSVs, esp matatus, keep your neighbour on check! He may be one of the criminals.

*IF YOU SUSPECT TO HAVE BEEN DRUGGED:*
1 - With your last energies, shout for help...most times unfortunately you may have lost your voice already!
2 - Drag yourself to the closest shop or Security Officer for help. 
3 - The effects wear off if you wash your face and hands. 
4 - Get to hospital as soon as possible. 
5. Report to the nearest police station, whenever you can, even if they do nothing, you will have done your part!
Our REQUEST, Please HELP OTHERS by passing on this information. 

Your Security starts with you.

06/08/2023, 3:41 pm - Agnes: Hi, jambo!

For borehole drilling with plastic casings - KES 6200 per meter

For borehole drilling with steel casings - KES 6700 per meter

This rate covers borehole construction (drilling, casings installation, gravel packing and development), and test pumping.
06/08/2023, 3:50 pm - Davie: Waaache story mingi, watuambie tutalipa how much tupate maji
06/08/2023, 4:38 pm - Agnes: Working with an average depth of 200 meters (from most boreholes in the area):

Borehole drilling with steel casings is KES 1,340,000. 

The maximum installation depth of plastic casings is 180 meters, so that negates the plastic casings option.

Installation of a pump system with solar energy is likely to cost approximately KES 1,200,000.

Also there's a hydrogeological survey done before drilling, complete with all permits at KES 85,000.

So the cumulative cost is KES 2,625,000

There might be other costs beyond this, like construction of a tank tower, plumbing or a drip irrigation system. So it's advisable to have at least KES 3,000,000 for a borehole project.

It is with heavy hearts that we come together once again, not in our initial role of providing medical support, but in a new and equally important mission. Our dear friend, *Paul Mutulu Muia*,  left us on September 9, 2023 while undergoing medical treatment at Shalom Hospital in Machakos, after a courageous battle with chronic kidney failure. Paul showed incredible strength and resilience throughout his health challenges, and now, as a community of friends, we want to honor his memory by ensuring he receives a dignified farewell.

With heartfelt gratitude.
